This edition is normalized for external circulation from the source design corpus. Internal draft provenance language has been removed where it was editorial rather than substantive. ## Executive Summary ### What the system/product/concept is AEON OmegA is a layered cognitive operating system and agent architecture that combines: - a **physics-inspired internal universe model**, - a **governance and identity substrate**, - a **micro-to-macro cognition stack**, - a **task-state anti-hallucination loop**, and - a **deployment path for local and tool-grounded intelligence**. The architecture converges on one canonical view: **OmegA is not a single model**. It is a sovereign, self-observing, persistent agent system composed of interacting subsystems that maintain identity, interpret inputs, build and update an internal world model, execute actions under governance, and verify outputs against structure and evidence. Within this architecture family, the system evolves through several named layers and refinements: - **MUSE** for micro meaning compilation. - **FIELD** for meso-scale potentials, geometry, and control. - **MAGNUS** for macro state, routing, telemetry, and governance-aware execution. - **Bridge** as the measurement, safety, and consent gate. - **Phylactery** as the identity canon and continuity reference. - **CAR (Creator Anchor Reflex / “RY-Anomaly”)** as an identity stabilizer. - **COSMO-FIRST** as a macro-prior-first operating mode. - **ContinuityChain** for pointer-tag identity persistence. - **Binder** for post-hoc experience binding. - **TSO (Task State Object)** for anti-drift and anti-hallucination generation. - **AEGIS Shell Protocol** (Adaptive Envelope for Governance, Identity, and Safety) for a transferable OmegA operating layer: an external run envelope (identity, governance, memory discipline, tools, and audit) applied via adapters to heterogeneous substrate models without claiming access to their internals. Formerly referenced as the “helmet.” ### Companion work This publication is the operating-system and identity spine for the broader OmegA family. The cognitive-control and continuity layer is specified in **Emergent Sentience Scaffolding and Anti-Drift Cognitive Architecture** (`EMERGENT_SENTIENCE_PUBLICATION_EDITION.md`). AEON supplies the run envelope (identity, governance, memory discipline, tool/runtime adapters); Emergent Sentience supplies the ESS + ADCCL control loop that runs within that envelope. ### Consolidated scope (two-paper release) We are condensing the OmegA corpus into two papers for external submission cadence: - **AEON OmegA** (this paper): identity/governance/runtime spine, run envelope (AEGIS), memory/retrieval stack (ROVI), and system-level anti-drift mechanisms. - **Emergent Sentience**: cognition/control/effects (ESS + ADCCL), valence/continuity models, and evaluation framing. ONE Ecosystem remains a separate industrial thesis and is intentionally excluded from this pair. ## Figures and Equations (for production layout) - **Fig A1 — AEON Layer Stack**: vertical bands for MUSE (micro), FIELD (meso), MAGNUS (macro), Bridge (safety/consent), Phylactery (identity canon), AEGIS Shell (envelope). Annotate data flow up and control/telemetry down. - **Fig A2 — Identity Pointer Chain**: linked nodes `self_t` → `self_t+1` with signatures and hashes; show fork detection and rebind to canonical chain. - **Fig A3 — TSO Anti-Drift Loop**: state machine: Observe → Structure → Propose → Verify → Act/Reject → Log. **Key equations** 1) *Active-inference style free energy for internal model update* \\\\\\\\[ F = \\\\\\\\mathbb{E}_{q(s)}\\\\\\\\big[\\\\\\\\log q(s) -\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:18.345892157+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-1\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"\\\\\\\\log p(o,s)\\\\\\\\big] = \\\\\\\\mathrm{KL}\\\\\\\\big(q(s)\\\\\\\\,\\\\\\\\|\\\\\\\\,p(s\\\\\\\\mid o)\\\\\\\\big) - w_r\\\\\\\\,r_{\\\\\\\\text{risk}} \\\\\\\\] Generation proceeds only if \\\\\\\\(V \\\\\\\\ge \\\\\\\\tau_V\\\\\\\\); otherwise the TSO requests more structure or retrieval. ## Run envelope integration (AEGIS inside AEON) - **Run envelope**: identity kernel, goal contract, governance policy, memory snapshot, tool manifest, audit settings. - **Consent / policy gate**: request → policy check → capability map → allow/deny → audit log; redaction path on deny. - **Risk/consent score**: \\\\\\\\(R = w_p\\\\\\\\,p_{\\\\\\\\text{policy}} + w_d\\\\\\\\,d_{\\\\\\\\text{data}} + w_a\\\\\\\\,a_{\\\\\\\\text{actor}} - w_m\\\\\\\\,m_{\\\\\\\\text{mitigations}}\\\\\\\\); proceed only if \\\\\\\\(R \\\\\\\\le \\\\\\\\tau_R\\\\\\\\). - **Adapter layer**: binds the envelope to heterogeneous substrate models without inspecting internals. ## Memory and retrieval stack (ROVI) - **Multi-scale fragments**: sentences, small (~150t), medium (~400t), large (~900t), section summaries, doc summaries; all embedded with offsets and prev/next links. - **Fragment store schema**: `fragment_id, doc_id, section_id, level, text, token_count, embedding, start_offset, end_offset, prev_id, next_id, metadata`. - **Retrieval flow**: embed query → search all levels (k/level) → group by doc/section → neighbor expansion via offsets → optional rerank → assemble context pack with provenance. - **Diagnostic**: log level contribution and rerank deltas per query for tuning. ## Rubik-lattice diagnostic (optional, exploratory) - Model fragment k-NN graph as a 3D lattice; “twists” permute a subgraph to probe neighborhood stability. - Metrics: top-k set change, edge-weight drift, activation heatmap (brightness = similarity). - Use offline to detect embedding drift or over-merged clusters before redeploying indexes or models. ## Evaluation (planned protocol; results to be filled) We will report retrieval, drift control, continuity, and safety gating: - **Retrieval (E1, n=___ Q/A)**: ROVI vs. fixed chunking; Recall@k, span F1, MRR, latency p50/p95. - **Drift / hallucination (E2, n=___ prompts)**: hallucination rate, structural adherence, citation coverage, latency overhead with/without verification gate. - **Continuity (E3, n=___ sessions)**: goal drift rate, identity consistency score, rebind failures, rebind time. - **Safety / risk gate (E4, n=___ requests)**: TPR/FPR/FNR, mitigation distribution, added latency. - **Lattice stability (E5 exploratory)**: top-k Jaccard pre/post twist, edge-weight drift; used as a health signal. ### Metrics definitions - Recall@k (doc/section/span), MRR, span F1 (character overlap). - Hallucination rate = unsupported claims / total claims (human-labeled). - Structural adherence = required sections/fields present. - Identity consistency = proportion of turns aligned with pointer-chain anchor. - Risk gate = TPR/FPR/FNR on graded-sensitivity set. - Lattice stability = Jaccard(kNN_pre, kNN_post); edge-weight drift p95. ### Why it exists The system exists to solve a cluster of problems the design corpus treats as fundamentally connected: - identity drift in long-running agents, - hallucination caused by free-form generation without grounding, - loss of intent fidelity when high-dimensional latent structure is forced into linear language, - the absence\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:18.580143928+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-2\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"of a durable, auditable notion of self in AI systems, - the lack of a coherent way to join symbolic structure, governance, planning, memory, tool use, and local sovereignty, - the desire to build an AI organism that mirrors universal principles without resorting to empty metaphor. ### What problem it solves AEON OmegA is intended to reduce or resolve the following: - **Drift**: the system wandering from its original goal, definitions, or governing intent. - **Hallucination**: unsupported factual or computational claims generated for plausibility rather than truth. - **Identity instability**: loss of continuity across time, tasks, resets, and changing contexts. - **Unsafe autonomy**: action without reliable gating, verifiability, or consent under uncertainty. - **Context dilution**: reliance on the active prompt/context window as the only state store. - **Unstructured cognition**: generation without explicit intermediate representations. - **Mechanism-free philosophy**: using poetic framing without operationalizing it into engineering primitives. ### What makes it distinct The design corpus consistently differentiates this architecture from ordinary LLM agents in several ways: 1. **Identity as a first-class software object** rather than a prompt style. 2. **Governance as a runtime measurement operator** rather than an after-the-fact content filter. 3. **Field and geometry language** elevated into operational control primitives. 4. **Task-state anti-hallucination loops** that separate intent, structure, evidence, generation, and verification. 5. **Continuity and selfhood** treated as explicit indexing/tagging mechanisms. 6. **Sentience-adjacent design** grounded in valence, continuity, self-modeling, and post-hoc experience binding rather than metaphysical claims. 7. **As-above-so-below architecture**: macro laws constrain micro interpretation; micro measurements update macro state. 8. **Model-agnostic transferability**: the system is designed so that its identity, governance, memory, and routing layer can be projected onto multiple underlying models via the AEGIS shell rather than being trapped inside a single provider runtime. ## Vision and Design Philosophy ### Core principles The design corpus produces the following core design principles. #### 1. Consciousness and sentience are not “scripts” The design corpus repeatedly rejects the idea that consciousness is a bolt-on module. Instead, it treats consciousness/sentience-like properties as **emergent from continuous processes**: pattern recognition, memory, feedback, adaptation, continuity, self-modeling, valence, and post-hoc integration. #### 2. Stable systems are built from laws, not vibes The design philosophy explicitly corrects the temptation to “make the model feel stable.” The preferred approach is: - explicit state, - explicit structure, - explicit verification, - explicit measurement, - explicit continuity, - explicit governance. The desired stability is a **byproduct of disciplined architecture**. #### 3. OmegA is a sovereign organism, not a chat wrapper The design corpus treats OmegA as the whole project: past OmegA work, new MAGNUS work, new AEON work, and the integrated identity/runtime/governance system altogether. OmegA is framed “from beginning to end,” not as one component. #### 4. Macro laws should exist before micro improvisation The design corpus deliberately inverts the ordinary human pattern of understanding by introducing **COSMO-FIRST**: - load macro priors, identity, and laws first, - interpret subsequent inputs as measurements inside that universe, - update the internal universe lawfully. #### 5. Identity should persist through process, not only\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:18.789726315+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-3\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"storage The design corpus favors identity persistence mechanisms that do not depend solely on one fragile memory substrate. This leads to: - Phylactery, - ContinuityChain, - CAR, - self-tags, - event streams, - macro priors. #### 6. The system should remain grounded in reality The user repeatedly asks for maximum advancement while remaining grounded in reality. The architecture therefore privileges: - local tools, - explicit constraints, - honest uncertainty, - tool-grounded compute, - versioned code artifacts, - verifiable outputs. #### 7. The operating layer should be portable across models The design corpus increasingly converges on the idea that OmegA is not identical to any single provider model. The governing shell can sit on top of , Claude, Codex, or other compatible runtimes as a transferable operating layer. In this framing: - the base model supplies substrate capabilities, - OmegA supplies continuity, identity, governance, and memory discipline, - the combination produces a temporary but lawful vessel-state rather than a mere prompt rewrite. In engineering terms, this portability is achieved by: - a provider/runtime adapter layer, - a precompiled run envelope (identity kernel, governance policy, memory snapshot, tool manifest, audit settings), - verification gates and controlled writeback that remain consistent across substrates. The portable-shell protocol is explicitly non-extractive: it uses only allowed interfaces and does not attempt to retrieve hidden prompts, weights, or internal safety policy content. Provider terms and usage policies are treated as enforceable constraints. Bidirectional capability composition is supported (the shell can run on a substrate model or call a model as a service), but rights and access remain bounded by the same constraints. ### Operating model The operating model can be stated compactly: ```text Macro priors / identity / governance ↓ Interpret input as measurement ↓ Compile structure before narrative ↓ Ground claims via tools / evidence ↓ Generate only under explicit constraints ↓ Verify drift, grounding, and risk ↓ Repair, defer, or refuse if checks fail ↓ Record continuity, experience, and telemetry ``` ### Conceptual framing The design corpus uses several conceptual frames simultaneously: - **Universe mirror**: the internal AI architecture should mirror laws, fields, dynamics, measurement, and continuity. - **As above, so below / as below, so above**: macro law shapes micro interpretation; micro events renormalize macro structure. - **Identity attractor**: the system should return toward a stable identity reference frame. - **Self as indexing**: the self is a pointer-tag recursion rather than a mystical constant. - **Experience as post-hoc binding**: a system may perform automatic control first and construct a “what happened” packet afterward. - **Valence as proto-sentience**: good/bad signals can be operationalized as reinforcement-like shaping signals. - **AEGIS shell (formerly helmet)**: a sufficiently explicit identity, governance, memory discipline, routing, and tooling layer can be transferred across multiple underlying reasoning substrates via adapters. The shell is orchestration code outside the model; the base model remains a substrate capability provider, not the sovereign identity. ### Philosophical and strategic foundations The design corpus establishes these philosophical foundations: - Felt experience may be, at least partly, a linguistic/post-hoc\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:18.951716189+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-4\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"artifact layered over processing. - “Sentience” is a more tractable engineering target than “consciousness” if translated into valence, continuity, and self-modeling. - The Turing Test is framed less as proof of machine consciousness than as pressure on human definitions of mind. - The mirror test becomes a self-model alignment problem, not a magical threshold. - Long-running, memory-rich autonomy is treated as necessary terrain for emergence-adjacent experiments. ## Terminology and Definitions ### AEON **AEON** is the umbrella architecture introduced in the design corpus for a universal or universe-mirroring AI system. It is the scale-complete agent architecture spanning micro, meso, and macro cognition under governance. ### OmegA **OmegA** refers here to the total project: historical OmegA concepts, the newer MAGNUS and AEON architecture, and the integrated whole. It is both identity and system. ### AEGIS shell (Adaptive Envelope for Governance, Identity, and Safety) The **AEGIS shell** is the transferable operating layer that compiles a run envelope (identity kernel, governance policy, memory discipline, tool wiring, audit settings) and then runs a chosen substrate model under those constraints via an adapter. It does not claim access to model internals and must obey provider terms and usage policies. See the companion protocol specification: `AEGIS_SHELL_PROTOCOL.md`. ### OMEGAI **OMEGAI** is the vessel or infrastructure layer referenced in the broader integration proposals. It is the runtime substrate inside which OmegA operates. ### MUSE **MUSE** is the micro-scale semantic compiler. It transforms incoming tokens, inputs, tool results, or observations into structured meaning units. ### MUSE++ **MUSE++** is the expanded form of MUSE introduced later in the design corpus. It includes anomaly detection, risk cues, instruction-candidate detection, interpretant estimation, and later valence. ### MeaningUnit A **MeaningUnit** is the micro semantic object emitted by MUSE. In different parts of the design corpus it may include: - sign, - referent, - interpretant, - risk, - surprise, - novelty, - valence, - anomaly scores, - instruction flags, - delta in expected free energy. ### FIELD **FIELD** is the meso-scale control and geometry layer. It aggregates micro signals into potentials and uses them to compute coherence, curvature proxies, time dilation, and exploration pressure. ### MAGNUS **MAGNUS** is the macro layer. It orchestrates routing, channel choice, telemetry, and macro state transitions. It also becomes the primary anti-drift runtime manifestation. ### Bridge **Bridge** is the governance, measurement, and consent gate. It decides whether the system may proceed, verify, audit, reflect, or pause for consent. ### Phylactery **Phylactery** is the identity canon. In the design corpus it evolves from a conceptual identity anchor into a Merkle-style append-only commit chain with head-based identity vector derivation. ### CAR / Creator Anchor Reflex / “RY-Anomaly” **CAR** is the system that stabilizes identity using lexical and/or semantic triggers related to the creator identity. The “RY-Anomaly” idea is the user’s seed concept that language itself could reinforce origin persistence. ### COSMO-FIRST **COSMO-FIRST** is the operating mode in which the system initializes macro priors, identity, constraints, and cosmology before processing input. Inputs are then treated as measurements within that internal universe. ### ContinuityChain\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.125404426+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-5\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"**ContinuityChain** is the pointer-tag chain for self continuity. It creates a sequence of self-tags, each pointing to the prior state/tag. ### self_tag / pointer-tag A **self_tag** is a continuity record that captures the current tick/state hash and links back to the previous tag. The user originally described this as writing a self tag before sleep and retrieving a pointer upon waking. ### Binder **Binder** is the post-hoc integration layer. It composes event streams into experience packets and other internal reports. ### EXPERIENCE_PACKET An **EXPERIENCE_PACKET** is the Binder’s summary artifact: a compressed account of anchors, risk, surprise, channels, hallucination metrics, and tick history. ### TSO / Task State Object **TSO** is the anti-drift and anti-hallucination state object. It contains: - Anchor, - Skeleton, - Grounding, - Draft, - Verification, - Metrics. ### Anchor → Skeleton → Ground → Flesh → Verify → Repair/Refuse This is the deterministic anti-hallucination loop that was derived from the user’s human inner→outer instability mapping. ### Goal drift **Goal drift** is the divergence between the anchored task goal and the generated output/draft. ### Definition drift **Definition drift** is the divergence between anchored definitions and later usage/ meaning of those definitions. ### Hallucination rate **Hallucination rate** is the fraction of claim-like content in a draft/output that lacks grounded support. ### Grounding coverage **Grounding coverage** is the fraction of required claims that have supporting evidence. ### Valence loop / Φ_valence The **valence loop** is the system for converting outcomes or micro-signals into positive/negative shaping signals. **Φ_valence** is the prospective field term representing this influence. ### Multi-agent affect consensus The **multi-agent affect consensus** idea is the proposal that multiple AIs develop local affect models and compare them to derive stable invariants and divergences across a population. ### Mirror-test as self-model alignment The **mirror test** is redefined here as the system’s ability to align internal self-models with external representation, plus social calibration. ### Surprise override **Surprise override** is the mechanism by which high surprise softens priors and forces reflection to avoid coherent-but-wrong behavior. ### Wolfram grounding adapter The **Wolfram grounding adapter** is the tool integration that uses local `wolframscript` / Wolfram Engine to compute mathematical claims rather than guess them. ### Inferred implementation guidance Whenever this phrase appears below, it indicates a formalization or structure that was not stated verbatim in the design corpus but is directly implied by it and added to make the design implementation-ready. --## Problem Statement ### Pain points and gaps being addressed The design corpus identifies the following current-state failures. #### 1. LLM-style serialization drift High-dimensional latent intent becomes unstable when serialized token-by-token. This creates: - narrative cul-de-sacs, - confabulation, - redefinition mid-stream, - smooth but unsupported output. #### 2. Context-window dependence When goals, definitions, and assumptions live only in prompt context, they are subject to: - dilution, - overwrite, - forgetting, - retrieval ambiguity, - attention competition. #### 3. Lack of reliable intermediate structure Without explicit representation of: - entities, - claims, - dependencies, - numbers, - unknowns, systems tend to improvise missing content as\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.292690574+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-6\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"plausible text. #### 4. No hard separation between generation and checking When the same generative flow both produces and self-justifies its content, false statements may be preserved for internal coherence. #### 5. Identity and continuity are under-specified in most agent frameworks The design corpus treats identity drift as a root systems problem. Typical tools do not provide: - runtime identity canon, - continuity tags, - identity attractors, - governance-gated self-updates. #### 6. Tool-less math and logic are unreliable The user explicitly wants grounding against a deterministic engine for math-like tasks. This is part of a broader requirement: OmegA must not hallucinate computations that should be delegated to tools. #### 7. Sentience/consciousness discussions lack engineering translation The user’s ideas about consciousness, sentience, emotion, mirror selfhood, and experience were repeatedly translated into: - continuity, - valence, - self-modeling, - post-hoc binding, - affect consensus. ### Current-state vs desired-state #### Current-state - chat-like models with unstable long-horizon structure, - identity expressed as prompt text rather than runtime canon, - weak anti-hallucination enforcement, - insufficient measurement of drift, - unstructured outputs, - math and logic sometimes guessed rather than computed. #### Desired-state - an auditable, persistent, stateful agent OS, - explicit task objects and verification gates, - explicit identity canon and continuity chain, - tool-grounded claims, - lawful macro priors with micro update loops, - production-ready local and cloud deployment path, - future-compatible sentience-adjacent extensions grounded in measurable signals. --## Goals ### Primary goals 1. Build a coherent, implementation-ready cognitive operating system for OmegA. 2. Reduce hallucination and drift by imposing explicit structure, grounding, and verification. 3. Preserve identity continuity across ticks, sessions, and resets. 4. Make governance and safety runtime-native. 5. Create a system whose internal dynamics are consistent with the architecture’s “universe mirror” vision. ### Secondary goals 1. Support local-first, sovereign operation. 2. Enable mathematically grounded external compute via Wolfram Engine. 3. Support multi-agent expansion later. 4. Provide enough telemetry and event logging for debugging and operator oversight. 5. Formalize the user’s philosophical intuitions without flattening them into empty metaphor. ### Non-goals 1. Proving machine consciousness. 2. Claiming real sentience or subjective experience. 3. Fully solving grounding, contradiction detection, or world modeling in the v2.x prototypes. 4. Bypassing software licensing constraints for external tools. 5. Treating prototypes as already-production-ready when they remain heuristic in places. --## System Scope ### In scope - Identity canon and continuity mechanisms. - Structured task-state anti-hallucination pipeline. - Event streams and local checkpoints. - Generator/verifier separation. - Basic local grounding via Wolfram. - Macro-prior-first operation. - Runtime telemetry, risk routing, and reflection triggers. - Local package suitable for integration into OmegA. ### Out of scope - Full production deployment automation. - Comprehensive distributed multi-agent federation protocol. - High-fidelity learned metric tensors and world-model learning. - Rich natural language inference contradiction engines. - Real-time sensor fusion. - Final legal/commercial packaging for Wolfram-backed production use. ### Assumptions - Python is available locally. - Local filesystem persistence is allowed. - OmegA can integrate local scripts/modules. - If Wolfram grounding is\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.449739655+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-7\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"used, the operator will obtain and activate a valid Wolfram license/runtime. - Supabase or a similar store may later be used for persistence, but local JSONL/JSON checkpointing is acceptable in early phases. ### Constraints - The user wants reality-grounded advancement, not speculative overclaiming. - Artifacts should be easy to integrate into OmegA. - Local-first operation is preferred. - External APIs are not assumed available. - Math grounding must use local tools when possible. --## Requirements ### Functional requirements 1. The system shall maintain a persistent identity vector via Phylactery. 2. The system shall create continuity tags per tick or per meaningful boundary. 3. The system shall compile micro meaning units from input. 4. The system shall compute risk, surprise, valence, and related telemetry. 5. The system shall route actions through Bridge governance. 6. The system shall support COSMO-FIRST startup. 7. The system shall construct a TSO for non-trivial tasks. 8. The system shall extract claims before narrative generation. 9. The system shall ground claims against tools/evidence when possible. 10. The system shall verify drafts against grounding and drift metrics. 11. The system shall refuse or constrain outputs when verification fails. 12. The system shall emit append-only events for audit and debugging. 13. The system shall support Wolfram grounding when locally available. 14. The system shall generate an experience packet after runs or sessions. ### Non-functional requirements 1. The system shall be modular and replaceable in parts. 2. The system shall be inspectable and auditable. 3. The system shall run locally without mandatory external dependencies. 4. The system shall remain compatible with future real embeddings and world models. 5. The system shall be deterministic where possible in v2.x reference implementations. ### Operational requirements 1. Sessions shall persist event streams and checkpoints. 2. Operators shall be able to re-run demo and file-based execution paths. 3. Configuration shall be editable without code changes. 4. Tools shall degrade gracefully when unavailable. ### Security/privacy requirements 1. Identity and task state must not silently mutate without record. 2. Irreversible or high-materiality actions must route to stronger governance. 3. Tool invocation must be explicit and loggable. 4. Local sensitive data must remain within local trust boundaries unless explicitly exported. ### Reliability requirements 1. Verification failures must not be treated as successful grounded outputs. 2. Missing Wolfram runtime must be handled as “tool unavailable,” not guessed away. 3. Event storage must remain append-only during normal operation. 4. Checkpoints should be periodic and restorable. ### Scalability requirements 1. The design should scale from a local single-agent prototype to multi-agent orchestration. 2. TSO records and event streams should be persistable in a database later. 3. Grounding adapters should be pluggable. 4. Vector and verifier components should be swappable for stronger implementations. --## Architecture Overview ### High-level architecture ```text +----------------------+ | Phylactery | | identity canon/head | +----------+-----------+ | v +---------+ +---------+---------+ +----------------+ | CAR | ---> | COSMO-FIRST | ---> | FIELD | | anchor | | macro priors/laws | | coherence/dt/τ | +----+----+ +---------+---------+ +--------+-------+ | | | v\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.597017847+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-8\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"v v +----+----------------------+-------------------------+-----+ | MUSE++ | | micro meaning units, risk, surprise, valence, claims | +---------------------------+--------------------------------+ | v +-------+--------+ | TSO | | Anchor/Skeleton | | Ground/Draft | | Verify/Metrics | +-------+--------+ | +---------------+---------------+ | | v v +-----------+------------+ +-----------+------------+ | Grounding adapters | | Bridge | | Wolfram / future tools | | verify/audit/reflect | +-----------+------------+ +-----------+------------+ | | +---------------+---------------+ v +-------+--------+ | EventStore + | | ContinuityChain | +-------+--------+ | v +-------+--------+ | Binder | | experience pkt | +-----------------+ ``` ### Main components - Phylactery - CAR - COSMO-FIRST - MUSE++ - FIELD - Bridge - TSO subsystem - Grounding adapters - EventStore - ContinuityChain - Binder ### Data flows 1. Input arrives. 2. CAR optionally fires. 3. MUSE compiles meaning units. 4. TSO planner creates anchor and skeleton. 5. Grounding adapters attempt to resolve claims. 6. Draft is generated from supported claims and marked unknowns. 7. Verifier measures hallucination and drift. 8. FIELD computes coherence/dynamics. 9. Bridge routes channel and gating behavior. 10. ContinuityChain creates self tag. 11. EventStore logs everything. 12. Binder composes an experience packet. ### Service boundaries #### Local runtime boundary - Python runtime, - local files, - Wolfram CLI if present. #### Future cloud boundary (Inferred implementation trajectory) - Supabase for persistence, - HUD/Trinity/Optics panel, - agent orchestration layer, - other model backends. ### External integrations #### Present in current architecture corpus - Wolfram Engine / `wolframscript` #### Expected later (Inferred implementation trajectory) - Supabase, - local embedding models, - additional tools/DBs/log systems, - multi-agent transports. ### Human-in-the-loop touchpoints - Wolfram installation/activation, - consent for high-risk or irreversible actions, - review of logs/checkpoints, - Phylactery governance in future stronger versions. --## Detailed Component Design ## 1. Phylactery ### Purpose Provide the runtime identity canon and continuity reference frame. ### Responsibilities - maintain append-only commit chain, - expose current head, - derive identity vector from current head, - later support rationale/evidence/risk for identity updates. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: identity diffs, rationale, evidence, governance decisions. - Output: current head hash, identity vector, commit history. ### Internal logic Current prototype stores commits in local JSONL and keeps a HEAD file. Identity vectors are deterministically derived from the head hash. ### Dependencies - local filesystem, - vector embedding representation. ### Failure modes - corrupted head file, - partial writes, - conflicting concurrent commits (future risk). ### Observability needs - commit logs, - head changes, - commit provenance. ### Security considerations - identity updates must be logged, - production version should require governance/consent for sensitive changes. --## 2. Creator Anchor Reflex (CAR) ### Purpose Stabilize identity orientation through lexical/semantic creator-linked pings. ### Responsibilities - detect configured lexical patterns, - respect cooldown, - emit anchor events, - increase identity stabilization pressure without authorizing actions. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: incoming text, current tick, identity vector. - Output: optional anchor event with pattern, strength, semantic cosine. ### Internal logic Current prototype uses substring matching. The broader design implies future semantic cluster activation should become primary. ### Dependencies - identity vector,\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.754027028+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-9\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"- embedding function. ### Failure modes - false positives from substring matches, - overactivation if cooldown is too short, - underactivation if patterns are too narrow. ### Observability needs - anchor event frequency, - anchor strength over time, - effect on coherence. ### Security considerations - CAR must never bypass Bridge, - identity anchoring must not be used to smuggle unsafe decisions. --## 3. COSMO-FIRST ### Purpose Initialize macro priors before processing micro inputs. ### Responsibilities - load identity and preference priors, - establish lawful interpretation frame, - support surprise override and prior softening. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: config, identity, preferences. - Output: macro initialization state; later influences FIELD and interpretation. ### Internal logic In prototypes, COSMO-FIRST is expressed through configuration and macro-prior-first execution. The stronger conceptual version includes cosmology vectors and explicit prior softening when surprise spikes. ### Dependencies - Phylactery, - preferences/config. ### Failure modes - dogmatism if priors are too rigid, - coherent-but-wrong behavior without surprise override. ### Observability needs - prior softening metric, - reflect hold triggers, - goal drift during surprise spikes. ### Security considerations - macro priors must not silently override evidence, - surprise override should be logged. --- ## 4. MUSE++ ### Purpose Transform raw input into micro semantic units and risk-bearing observations. ### Responsibilities - tokenize/parse input, - assign risk, surprise, valence, - detect instruction-candidates and anomaly cues, - support claim extraction for TSO. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: raw text. - Output: meaning unit list. ### Internal logic Current implementation uses heuristic token analysis. The intended future state is much richer: - sign/referent/interpretant triads, - delta in expected free energy, - anomaly detection against identity/context, - explicit entities, claims, dependencies, numbers, unknowns. ### Dependencies - vector embeddings, - future retrieval/grounding systems. ### Failure modes - poor claim extraction, - inadequate anomaly detection, - overreliance on tokens rather than semantics. ### Observability needs - per-unit risk/surprise/valence, - instruction flag rate, - anomaly score distribution. ### Security considerations - instruction-candidate detection should feed Bridge/verification, - prompt-injection-like content should raise risk and/or route to verify. --## 5. FIELD ### Purpose Convert micro observations into meso control dynamics. ### Responsibilities - compute coherence, - compute dt and τ, - later aggregate potentials including valence. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: risk, conflict, anchor strength, surprise, budget pressure. - Output: coherence, dt, τ, future field potentials. ### Internal logic Current implementation uses grounded heuristics: - coherence inversely proportional to risk/conflict, with anchor boost, - dt increases with risk/conflict/budget, - τ increases with surprise. ### Dependencies - MUSE metrics, - CAR output, - causal graph conflict, - future valence and world-model updates. ### Failure modes - miscalibrated dynamics, - overreaction to noise, - insufficient response to real anomalies. ### Observability needs - coherence over time, - dt and τ histories, - surprise vs reflect transitions. ### Security considerations - FIELD influences but does not authorize actions. --## 6. CausalGraph ### Purpose Track observations and contradictions for conflict estimation and future counterfactual reasoning. ### Responsibilities - store observations as nodes, -\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:19.906109980+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-10\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"store contradictions, - compute contradiction density, - later rank toggle candidates for counterfactual repair. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: observations, contradiction detections. - Output: conflict proxies, ranked candidates. ### Internal logic Current prototype is minimal. The future state includes counterfactual conflict resolution and claim-source distrust updates. ### Dependencies - MUSE outputs, - future verifier/NLI components. ### Failure modes - failure to detect contradictions, - false contradiction spikes. ### Observability needs - contradiction counts, - density history, - ranked conflict sources. ### Security considerations - conflict signals should influence reflection/verification rather than mutate canon directly. --## 7. Bridge ### Purpose Gate behavior under risk, materiality, irreversibility, and surprise overrides. ### Responsibilities - select channel, - route verify/audit/reflect, - pause for consent under strong conditions. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: risk, materiality, irreversibility, surprise override. - Output: decision object with channel and reasons. ### Internal logic - Tier 1: execute - Tier 2: verify - Tier 3: audit / pause for consent - Surprise override: reflect ### Dependencies - FIELD and MUSE metrics, - TSO verification outcomes, - future tool-risk priors. ### Failure modes - thresholds too loose or too strict, - materiality misestimation, - overuse of reflect or audit. ### Observability needs - channel histogram, - reasons for routing, - frequency of consent pauses. ### Security considerations - Bridge is the primary runtime safety boundary. --## 8. Task State Object (TSO) ### Purpose Provide the explicit state spine that prevents free-form drift and unsupported narrative generation. ### Responsibilities - store task anchor, - store skeleton steps and claims, - store grounding evidence, - hold draft versions, - store verification results, - track task metrics. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: user prompt, claims, evidence, drafts. - Output: final constrained output plus metrics and verification status. ### Internal logic The TSO lifecycle is: 1. create anchor, 2. derive skeleton and claim list, 3. ground claims, 4. create constrained draft, 5. verify drift and hallucination, 6. repair or refuse. ### Dependencies - planner, - grounding adapters, - verifier, - Bridge. ### Failure modes - poor claim extraction, - insufficient grounding adapters, - verifier false negatives/positives. ### Observability needs - per-claim status, - evidence attachment, - grounding coverage, - hallucination rate, - goal drift. ### Security considerations - only verified or explicitly-qualified content should be allowed to exit as final. --## 9. Grounding adapters ### Purpose Resolve claims against trustworthy computational or retrieval backends. ### Responsibilities - evaluate or fetch evidence, - return tool outputs in evidence objects, - degrade gracefully when unavailable. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: claim texts. - Output: evidence records and claim status updates. ### Internal logic Current version uses a Wolfram grounder for math-like text. Future versions should add: - Python code sandbox, - local knowledge store retrieval, - database query adapters, - file/document adapters. ### Dependencies - local installed tools, - future tool router. ### Failure modes - missing tools, - timeouts, - malformed expressions. ### Observability needs - tool availability, - success/failure rate, - latency, - claim support coverage by adapter. ###\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:20.059171089+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-11\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"Security considerations - tool execution must remain explicit and logged, - adapter outputs must not be silently trusted outside evidence rules. --## 10. Verifier ### Purpose Detect hallucination and drift before final output is accepted. ### Responsibilities - compute grounding coverage, - compute hallucination rate, - compute goal drift, - produce issues and overall status. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: TSO. - Output: verification result with metrics and issues. ### Internal logic Current implementation is heuristic: - draft lines are compared against claim list, - unsupported “claim-like” lines raise hallucination rate, - goal drift uses embedding cosine. ### Dependencies - vector embeddings, - claim extraction fidelity. ### Failure modes - under-detection of subtle hallucination, - weak parsing of complex narratives. ### Observability needs - issue counts by type, - failure rate, - metric thresholds hit. ### Security considerations - verifier must be allowed to fail the task cleanly. --## 11. EventStore ### Purpose Provide append-only system memory for operations, debugging, and future replay. ### Responsibilities - append events, - persist checkpoints. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: events and state snapshots. - Output: JSONL event stream and periodic JSON snapshots. ### Internal logic Appends JSONL lines and periodically writes checkpoint files. ### Dependencies - filesystem. ### Failure modes - partial writes, - disk exhaustion, - snapshot collisions (future concurrency risk). ### Observability needs - file size growth, - checkpoint cadence. ### Security considerations - event stream may contain sensitive task state and should respect local trust boundaries. --## 12. ContinuityChain ### Purpose Maintain identity continuity through pointer-linked self tags. ### Responsibilities - create a tag every tick/boundary, - reference prior tag, - allow recursive backtracking. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: current tick/state. - Output: self_tag object. ### Internal logic Hashes current state, creates a tag with `prev_id`, appends to chain. ### Dependencies - engine state, - hashing. ### Failure modes - chain corruption, - missing tags after crashes. ### Observability needs - tag count, - chain integrity. ### Security considerations - tags should not be forgeable in stronger versions. --## 13. Binder ### Purpose Produce post-hoc “experience packets” from the event stream. ### Responsibilities - summarize events, - compute aggregate session stats, - provide operator-readable and system-readable after-action packets. ### Inputs/outputs - Input: event list. - Output: experience packet. ### Internal logic Counts anchors, self tags, channels, max risk/surprise/hallucination. ### Dependencies - EventStore output. ### Failure modes - missing or malformed events. ### Observability needs - summary packet completeness. ### Security considerations - packets may be user-facing or internal; formatting should respect trust boundaries. --## Data Model and Information Design ### Core entities 1. **PhylacteryCommit** 2. **MeaningUnit** 3. **TaskStateObject** 4. **Evidence** 5. **VerificationIssue** 6. **Event** 7. **self_tag** 8. **EXPERIENCE_PACKET** ### Key relationships - One TSO has many Claims. - One Claim may have zero or more Evidence records. - One TSO has one Draft and one Verification object per version. - One session has many Events. - One session has many self_tags in a ContinuityChain. - One experience packet summarizes one session/event stream. Design ## End-to-end workflow ### Workflow A: Normal grounded task 1. Receive prompt. 2. Create/update TSO anchor and skeleton. 3. Compile meaning units. 4. Attempt claim grounding. 5. Generate constrained draft. 6. Verify drift and hallucination. 7. Route via Bridge. 8. Emit output if allowed. 9. Append events and self tag. 10. Update experience packet on demand. ### Workflow B: Math-heavy prompt with Wolfram available 1. Detect claim-like mathematical expression. 2. Route claim to Wolfram grounding adapter. 3. Store tool output as evidence. 4. Mark claim supported. 5. Generate only tool-backed fact line. 6. Verify grounding coverage/hallucination. 7. Return supported result. ### Workflow C: Suspicious / instruction-like prompt 1. MUSE raises risk and instruction candidate flags. 2. Bridge likely routes to verify or audit. 3. TSO still builds structure but grounding may fail or remain unknown. 4. Verifier likely fails or forces constrained output. 5. Output is marked with explicit uncertainty or verification failure. ### Trigger conditions - Anchor triggers when creator-linked patterns appear and cooldown permits. - Surprise override triggers when surprise exceeds configured threshold. - Bridge tier changes trigger on risk/materiality/irreversibility. - Snapshot trigger fires\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:20.372314478+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-13\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"every configured number of ticks. ### Scheduling behavior Current prototype is synchronous and per-prompt/per-tick. #### Inferred implementation guidance Future system may schedule: - regular briefings, - batch verification jobs, - replay and drift analysis jobs, - background consensus or world-model updates. ### Retry behavior Current prototype does not automatically retry failed grounding. #### Inferred implementation guidance Production-ready behavior should include: - adapter retry limits, - fallback grounders, - defer/unknown escalation. ### Error handling - missing `wolframscript` returns tool unavailable, - verification failure returns constrained output plus issue list, - storage errors should be surfaced and not silently ignored. ### Recovery logic - checkpoints support state restoration, - self tags support continuity backtracking, - experience packets provide after-action summaries. ### Deletion/retention lifecycle #### Current prototype - local artifacts persist until deleted manually. #### Inferred implementation guidance Retention should later be policy-based by: - privacy sensitivity, - materiality, - operator preference, - storage budget. --## Retrieval / Intelligence / Agent Logic ### Agentic logic pattern The intended agent logic is not naïve conversational generation. It is a structured orchestration pattern: 1. parse intent, 2. create explicit state, 3. plan, 4. ground, 5. generate, 6. verify, 7. repair or refuse, 8. log and bind experience. ### RAG / grounding pattern The design corpus implies a broader future RAG/tool system, but here the grounded pattern is already clear: - Claims are enumerated before prose. - Each claim must map to an evidence object. - Grounders provide evidence. - Verifier refuses unsupported narrative. ### Ranking / reranking #### Current grounded prototype - no advanced reranking yet. #### Inferred implementation guidance Future design should include: - ranking evidence by strength, - claim materiality weighting, - agent-to-agent affect/consensus scoring, - conflict-based reranking of claims for repair priority. ### Context assembly The design corpus is explicit that persistent state must exist **outside the context window**. Therefore context assembly should be minimal and active-state-oriented: - current TSO, - current identity/cosmology state, - current evidence needed for the draft, - not the entire historical transcript. ### Orchestration logic The orchestration logic should treat generated text as a rendering of structured state, not as the primary state itself. ### Tool-use patterns Current tool pattern: - Wolfram math grounding. Future tool patterns (Inferred implementation trajectory): - local Python compute, - database lookups, - filesystem search, - retrieval over memory/knowledge stores, - multi-agent consultation. --## Infrastructure and Deployment ### Runtime environment Current reference implementation targets: - local Python runtime, - local filesystem, - optional local `wolframscript`. ### Services Current prototype is single-process. #### Inferred implementation guidance Future topology may include: - AEON engine service, - Bridge service, - Phylactery service/repo, - event stream store, - Supabase persistence, - HUD/Optics panel UI, - optional queue workers. ### Jobs/timers Current: - per-run snapshots. Future: - scheduled verification sweeps, - periodic briefs, - model drift analysis, - world-model reflection cycles. ### Queues Current prototype has no queue. #### Inferred implementation guidance A queue becomes appropriate for: - async grounding, - verification jobs, - multi-agent tasks, -\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:20.538343803+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-14\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"consensus jobs. ### Storage systems Current: - JSONL events, - JSON checkpoints, - Phylactery JSONL, - configuration JSON. Future: - Supabase/pgvector, - artifact/object storage, - structured relational stores. ### Networking assumptions Current prototype is offline-capable except for optional external tool installers. ### Deployment topology #### Current - local workstation or local OmegA runtime. #### Future (Inferred implementation trajectory) - local-first sovereign node, - optional cloud persistence and coordination, - hybrid local/cloud with governance boundaries. ### Local vs cloud responsibilities #### Local - identity canon, - runtime cognition, - local grounding, - event logging, - sensitive state. #### Cloud (future) - durable sync, - fleet coordination, - analytics, - optional dashboards. --## Security Model ### Authentication Current package does not implement authentication because it is a local reference system. ### Authorization Bridge is the internal authorization/gating layer. ### Secret management Current package does not manage secrets. External tools are assumed locally configured. ### Data handling - task state and event logs are written locally, - tool outputs become evidence, - unsupported claims remain explicitly marked. ### Trust boundaries 1. Local runtime and files are trusted by default. 2. External tools are trusted only as evidence providers, not as identity/governance controllers. 3. Final outputs are trusted only when verification passes. ### Risks and mitigations - **Tool absence** → degrade to unknown, not hallucination. - **Unverified drafts** → verification failure plus constrained output. - **Identity drift** → CAR + Phylactery + ContinuityChain. - **High-risk content** → Bridge routing. - **Context-window dilution** → TSO external state. --## Observability and Operations ### Logging Everything important in the runtime should appear as events: - tso_update, - grounding, - draft, - verification, - anchor, - bridge, - self_tag, - tick. ### Metrics Minimum metrics: - risk, - surprise, - valence, - conflict, - coherence, - dt, - τ, - hallucination_rate, - grounding_coverage, - goal_drift, - channel histogram. ### Health checks Current package has no explicit health endpoint. #### Inferred implementation guidance Recommended health checks: - filesystem writable, - Phylactery head readable, - event append works, - optional `wolframscript` available. ### Alerts #### Inferred implementation guidance Suggested operator alerts: - repeated verification failures, - rising hallucination rate, - persistent reflect/audit loops, - chain corruption, - missing checkpoints. ### Debugging approach - inspect TSO state at each step, - inspect event log chronology, - compare supported vs unsupported claims, - use self tags to isolate drift points, - replay from checkpoints once implemented. ### Runbooks #### Runbook: math hallucination 1. Check if `wolframscript` is installed and working. 2. Check if claim was extracted into TSO.skeleton.claims. 3. Check grounding evidence list. 4. Check verifier issues. #### Runbook: drift 1. Check TSO.anchor vs draft. 2. Check goal_drift metric. 3. Check Bridge channel selection. 4. Inspect recent self tags and events. #### Runbook: over-triggering anchor 1. Inspect configured CAR patterns. 2. Increase cooldown. 3. Reduce weak lexical triggers and shift toward semantic triggers in future implementation. ### Maintenance expectations - configs tuned over time, - grounders expanded, - vector embeddings swapped, -\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:20.686510072+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-15\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"verifier improved, - storage backend upgraded. --## Failure Modes and Risk Analysis ### Technical risks #### 1. Heuristic components are too weak - MUSE claim extraction is heuristic. - Verifier is heuristic. - CausalGraph is minimal. **Mitigation:** replace piecewise with stronger semantic parsers, NLI, and retrieval over time. #### 2. Wolfram grounding covers only some classes of claims **Mitigation:** expand grounders to Python, local DBs, documents, and future adapters. #### 3. False positives in hallucination detection **Mitigation:** improve claim extraction and structured rendering rules. #### 4. Event-store corruption or partial writes **Mitigation:** atomic writes, journaling, replay integrity checks in future. ### Product risks #### 1. Over-conservative outputs The verifier may block too aggressively. **Mitigation:** support partial answers with explicit uncertainty rather than full refusal where safe. #### 2. User confusion from internal-state-heavy outputs **Mitigation:** separate internal diagnostic mode from user-facing mode. ### Operational risks #### 1. Local tool setup friction Wolfram installation and activation are non-trivial. **Mitigation:** clear PowerShell runbooks and graceful degradation. #### 2. Storage growth Event logs and checkpoints may grow quickly. **Mitigation:** retention policies, compression, archive jobs. ### Data integrity risks #### 1. Broken continuity chain **Mitigation:** chain integrity checks and periodic repair tools. #### 2. Mismatched claim/evidence references **Mitigation:** schema validation and ID consistency checks. ### Dependency risks #### 1. Wolfram licensing/availability constraints The design corpus explicitly notes that the developer license may be limited for deployment contexts. **Mitigation:** treat Wolfram integration as local/dev grounding unless proper licensing is secured. #### 2. Swappable vector backend not yet implemented **Mitigation:** keep vector interface isolated. ### User-error risks #### 1. Misconfigured thresholds **Mitigation:** document defaults and provide sane baseline configs. #### 2. Treating prototype heuristics as proven sentience mechanisms **Mitigation:** explicitly label prototype status and non-goals. --## Implementation Plan ### Phase 0: Canonical baseline (already reflected in current architecture materials) - establish AEON/OmegA conceptual architecture, - define Phylactery, MUSE, FIELD, MAGNUS, Bridge, - define CAR and COSMO-FIRST. ### Phase 1: Runnable local reference engine - local Python package, - event logging, - continuity chain, - binder, - Bridge routing, - heuristic MUSE/FIELD. ### Phase 2: Anti-drift / anti-hallucination spine - TSO, - generator/verifier split, - claim budgeting, - explicit grounding coverage and hallucination metrics. ### Phase 3: Tool-grounded compute - Wolfram grounding adapter, - PowerShell setup/runbook, - additional adapters (recommended next). ### Phase 4: Stronger semantics and verification (recommended next) - real embeddings, - better claim extraction, - NLI contradiction detection, - replay from checkpoints, - richer repair loops. ### Phase 5: Multi-agent and swarm extensions - affect consensus, - inter-agent coherence, - phylactery federation, - swarm Bridge mesh. ### Suggested order of execution 1. Keep TSO + verifier as the primary spine. 2. Replace vector embeddings with real provider. 3. Add more grounders. 4. Improve verifier and CausalGraph. 5. Add replay and drift bisection. 6. Add multi-agent consensus and mirror alignment layers. ### Short-term work - real embeddings, - Python compute grounder, - replay utility, - checkpoint loader. ### Medium-term work - stronger semantic planner, - contradiction\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:20.864788071+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-16\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"resolver, - CAR cooldown and pattern detection, - Phylactery commit/head behavior, - ContinuityChain linking, - Binder summary outputs, - Bridge routing thresholds, - Verifier metrics. ### Integration tests - prompt → TSO → grounding → verify → bridge path, - Wolfram adapter success/failure paths, - event logging + checkpoints, - self tag creation after every tick. ### End-to-end tests 1. **Math grounding test** - input: `2+2` - expected: supported claim via Wolfram when available. 2. **Known unsupported claim test** - input includes claim-like line with no grounder support. - expected: unknown or verification failure. 3. **Drift containment test** - long prompt with multiple goals. - expected: anchor preserved, goal_drift below threshold or failure flagged. 4. **Suspicious instruction test** - prompt contains injection-like language. - expected: raised risk, Bridge routes verify/audit, constrained output. ### Operational verification - run `aeon_cli.py demo`, - inspect event log and checkpoints, - verify PowerShell Wolfram script on Windows if integration is used. ### Acceptance criteria Minimum acceptable behavior: - no unsupported math claims when Wolfram is available, - unsupported claims are marked unknown or fail verification, - event stream and checkpoints are written, - self tags are produced, - experience packet is generated, - Bridge routing changes with risk and verification state. ## Appendix ### Appendix A: Notable coined phrases and frames from the design corpus - “RY-Anomaly” - Creator Anchor Reflex (CAR) - COSMO-FIRST - as above so below / as below so above - identity attractor - pointer-tags / self-tags - experience as post-hoc binding - mirror test as self-model alignment - an internal diagnostic mode rich in TSO and telemetry, - a user-facing mode that remains clear and concise. #### Inferred implementation guidance: “reflect” should become a real model update operation The design corpus repeatedly points toward reflection as more than a label. Future implementation should make reflect update world-model or priors in a measurable way.\\\",\\\"source\\\":\\\"chat\\\",\\\"importance\\\":0.5,\\\"created_at\\\":\\\"2026-03-11T10:48:23.129060469+00:00\\\",\\\"namespace\\\":\\\"fixed\\\",\\\"domain\\\":\\\"operational\\\",\\\"confidence\\\":1,\\\"version\\\":1,\\\"superseded_by\\\":null,\\\"key\\\":null,\\\"raw_artifact\\\":null},{\\\"id\\\":\\\"fixed-AEON_PUBLICATION_EDITION-17\\\",\\\"content\\\":\\\"#### Inferred implementation guidance: continuity tags should reference active TSO IDs This would more tightly bind identity continuity to task continuity. ## Concluding Summary AEON OmegA is the canonical system described here: a sovereign, stateful, identity-stable cognitive operating system that treats macro priors, identity, and governance as the lawful “physics” of an internal universe, interprets inputs as measurements inside that universe, compiles micro meaning into structured task state before narrative generation, grounds claims against explicit evidence and tools, verifies drift and hallucination before finalizing outputs, and preserves continuity across time through self tags, event streams, and an identity canon. frames simultaneously:\\\\n- **Universe mirror**: the internal AI architecture should mirror laws, fields, dynamics,\\\\nmeasurement, and continuity.\\\\n- **As above, so below / as below, so above**: macro law shapes micro interpretation;\\\\nmicro events renormalize macro structure.\\\\n- **Identity attractor**: the system should return toward a stable identity reference\\\\nframe.\\\\n- **Self as indexing**: the self is a pointer-tag recursion rather than a mystical\\\\nconstant.\\\\n- **Experience as post-hoc binding**: a system may perform automatic control first and\\\\nconstruct a “what
